Identifying Faulty Definitions in Relational Terms
Author critiques faulty definitions of relational terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify faulty definitions in relational terms by checking whether the differentia captures the essential specific relation.

Core Idea
A correct definition of a relational term must capture the exact relation, not just any relation.

The author presents several examples of definitions that go wrong because they miss the specific relation. For instance, defining 'sight' as having two relations (to seer and seen) fails to capture that sight is an instrument for seeing, not just any relation. This lesson will give you a method to spot such errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the passage. For example, 'sight' (al-basar).
2
Extract the proposed definition
What is being said about it? For sight: it is something with a relation to the seer and the seen.
3
Check if the definition captures the specific essence
Ask: Does the definition tell us what makes sight uniquely sight? The author says sight is an instrument by which the animal sees colors through sight. The relation to the seen is essential to its identity, not just an added relation.
4
Test with counterexamples
If the definition fails to exclude non-instances or include all instances, it is faulty. For passion ('ishq), defining it as 'desire for intercourse' fails because intense passion reduces that desire.
5
Classify the error type
Determine if the fault is an omitted essential relation, a misplaced relation, or a missing differentia. For sight, the relation was generic; the specific instrumental relation was omitted.
This helps in constructing correct definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطرف الآخر. فإن علاقة الموافقة المشابهة هي مع الموافقة التي في الكيفية لا إلى ذات الكيفية بما هي كيفية؛ وذلك المعنى قائم في الكيفية. وقد يقدم أن هذا النحو من الوجود الخاص غير معتبر في قولنا إن المضاف الحقيقي لا وجود له غير ما هو به مضاف، والغرض في قولنا بالقياس إنما هو متجه إلى معنى أعم من المضاف وهو كونه موجودًا أو ذا ماهية.
والمثال الآخر أن العلم منه نظري، ومنه عملي؛ فالعلم شيء ذو إضافة لذلك النظري والعملي. وأما النحو فهو نوع منه لا فصل فيقال في حده إنه علم لما يعرض للغة من جهة كذا وكذا؛ وفصله إضافي لا محالة، وفرق بين أن يقول إن الفصل مضاف، وبين أن يقول إنه مضاف إضافة خاصة، وموضع آخر أنه قد يكون لبعض المضافات بالمعنى العام إضافتان إلى الجانبين؛ وربَّما كان أحدهما بالحقيقة، والآخر بنوع من العرض فإذا لم تكن الإضافة واقعة إلى الشيء ينبغي أن يكون إليه. ومن الجهة التي تنبغي لم يكن التحديد جيدا مثلا إذا حد البصر الذي له إضافة إلى المُبصِر وإلى المُبصر لكنه إنما هو بصر لأنه يبصر به شيء ما فلا يمكن يتوهم البصر بصرا إلا وهو الذي يمكن به من تحقق المبصر بالنظر. ولا يبعد أن يتوهم بصرًا مفردًا ليس لشيء آخر فهو بصر لنفسه لا على أنه آلة لغيره فيكون تعلقه بالمبصر أمرًا في هويته، وتعلقه بمبصر هو البتة أمرًا لازمًا؛ فيجب إذن أن يراعى في التحديد فيقال إنه آلة بها يبصر الحيوان الألوان بالنظر . وعلى هذا إذا كان للشيء إضافة ما . وأما قولهم في تحديد الفهم إنه ملكة للنفس استعداد به نحو سرعة إدراك ما يرد عليها فذلك لا يصح لما أن الفهم أو لا ملكة لجزء ما للنفس وهي القوة الفكرية؛ ثمَّ للنفس ثمَّ للإنسان. وكذلك قولهم في العشق إنه شهوة الجماع؛ والعشق إذا اشتدَّ نقصت شهوة الجماع. وكذلك في النار إنها ألطف الأجسام؛ إذ اللهيب أكثف من نار البرق وهو أولى بالنارية من نار البرق. وعلى هذا فإن التحديد الفاسد متعدد غاية التعداد.
The other side. For the relation of accordance and similarity is with the accordance that is in the quality, not to the essence of quality as it is a quality; and that meaning subsists in the quality. And it may be presented that this type of particular existence is not considered in our statement that the real relative has no existence other than that by which it is relative, and the intent in our statement by analogy is directed to a meaning more general than the relative, which is its being existent or having an essence. Another example: knowledge is of two kinds: theoretical and practical. Knowledge is something having relation to that theoretical and practical. As for grammar, it is a type of it, not a differentia, so it is said in its definition that it is knowledge of what occurs to language from such-and-such aspect; and its differentia is relational necessarily, and there is a difference between saying that the differentia is relative and saying that it is relative in a particular relation. And another place: it may be that some relatives in the general sense have two relations to two sides; perhaps one of them is real and the other is a kind of accident. So when the relation does not occur to the thing to which it ought to be, and from the aspect which it ought to be, the definition is not good. For example, if one defines sight, which has a relation to the seer and to the seen, but it is sight only because something is seen by it; so it is impossible to conceive of sight as sight except that by which the seen is realized through sight. And it is not far-fetched to conceive of a single sight not for something else, so it is sight for itself, not as an instrument for another; so its relation to the seen is in its identity, and its relation to a seen thing is a necessary matter. So it is necessary to observe in the definition and say that it is an instrument by which the animal sees colors through sight. And likewise if something has some relation. As for their statement in defining understanding that it is a faculty of the soul having a readiness towards quick perception of what occurs to it, that is not correct because understanding is first a faculty of a part of the soul, which is the intellectual power; then for the soul; then for the human. And likewise their statement about passion that it is the desire for sexual intercourse; and passion when intense, the desire for sexual intercourse decreases. And likewise regarding fire that it is the subtlest of bodies; for the flame is denser than lightning fire, and it is more deserving of being fire than lightning fire. And upon this, faulty definition is manifold to the utmost extent.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage presents several examples of faulty definitions (al-tahdid al-fasid) from various domains, illustrating common errors. The author begins by discussing relational terms (al-mudaf), noting that a definition must capture the specific relation and not just a general one. He then offers specific examples: (1) Knowledge ('ilm) is defined as having both theoretical and practical aspects, but the definition should specify the relation; (2) Grammar (al-nahw) is defined as knowledge of what occurs to language, but its differentia is relational; (3) Sight (al-basar) must be defined as an instrument by which the animal sees colors, not just as having two relations; (4) Understanding (al-fahm) cannot be defined as a mere faculty because it is specific to a part of the soul; (5) Passion (al-'ishq) as desire for intercourse fails because intense desire reduces the desire; (6) Fire (al-nar) as the subtlest body fails because flame is denser than lightning fire yet more fiery. The point is that faulty definitions are extremely numerous.

Key Terms
المضاف
التحديد الفاسد
الفصل

Key Takeaway
A correct definition of a relational term must capture the specific relation that constitutes its essence, not just any relation or a partial description.

Classification of Definition Errors: Increase and Decrease
Author classifies errors in definition as excess or deficiency, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between definition errors of increase and decrease, and identify each in a given definition.

Core Idea
A correct definition must include all essential differentiae and nothing superfluous.

In this passage, the author systematically classifies two fundamental errors in definition: including unnecessary elements (increase) and omitting essential ones (decrease). Understanding these errors enables precise evaluation of definitions used in Islamic sciences, such as in usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and its proposed definition
Look at the examples: 'the beautiful' defined as 'what is pleasant to hearing and sight', 'the existent' defined as 'what can act and be acted upon', 'wind' defined as 'movement of air', 'earthquake' as 'movement of the earth's body', and 'will' as 'inclination towards the good'. Note the proposed definitions.
2
Check for error of increase
For the definition of 'beautiful', see if both conditions (pleasant to hearing AND sight) are necessary. If both are required, then something pleasant only to hearing would not be beautiful, yet it is. If both are not required, one is superfluous. This is an error of increase.
The author shows that including mutually opposite or unnecessary elements leads to contradiction or redundancy.
3
Check for error of decrease
For the definition of 'wind' as 'movement of air', note that it lacks specifying differentiae like magnitude or direction. Similarly, 'earthquake' as 'movement of the earth's body' omits how and how much. Omitting essential differentiae is an error of decrease.
The author cites Aristotle's Topics: omission of a differentia fails to capture the essence.
4
Apply to the definition of 'will'
The definition 'inclination of desire towards the good' is incomplete because will can also incline towards apparent good that is not truly good. The missing differentia is 'towards the good in appearance'.
This exemplifies the error of decrease, as the specifying differentia is omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : ومن أمثال هذه المواضع ما يكون الخطأ في التحديد بحسب الزيادة والنقصان والكل والجزء والجمع بحرف الواو وغير ذلك
أما بحسب الزيادة فمثل ما يورد في الحد أمران متنافعان كما يقال إن الحسن هو اللذيذ عند السمع واللذيذ عند البصر؛ والموجود هو الذي يمكن أن يفعل وأن ينفعل . ثمّ من المعلوم أن كل حسن فهو لذيذ عند السمع وعند البصر معا لكن اللذيذ عند البصر وحده حسن فهو حسن لا حسن. وكذلك اللذيذ عند السمع وحده. وبالجملة إذا كان كل واحد منهما شرطًا للصحة كان اللذيذ عند البصر مثلا لا يكون حسناً . وإذا لم يكن شرطًا كان أحدهما خارجا عن ماهية الحد فكان زائدا . وأما بحسب النقصان فمثل ما لا يورد فيه ما يخصه ويميزه كما هو فيقال مثلا إن الريح حركة هواء ولم يقلب أي مبلغ، أو يقال إن الزلزلة حركة جرم الأرض ولم يقل كم هو وكيف هو؛ وهذا يعود إلى إغفال فصل. وقد قيل في التعليم الأول في هذا المقام لأنه إذا أغفل فصلا من هذه الفصول لم تصف ماهية ذلك الشيء. وهذا يدل على أن المذهب الحق هو أن ماهية ذلك الشيء إنما يتم بكمال صفات ذاته؛ وإن الجنس وحده لا يدل على ماهية نوع واحد.
ومن الأمثلة لهذه المواضع ما قيل في حد الإرادة إنها انبعاث سوق نحو الخير، ولا يقال نحو الخير في الظاهر فإنه قد يراد ما ليس خيرًا حقيقيا ؛ وهذا
Section: Among such topics are that the error in definition occurs according to increase and decrease, the whole and the part, and combination with the letter 'and' and other things. As for increase, it is like when two mutually opposites are included in the definition, as when it is said that the beautiful is what is pleasant to hearing and pleasant to sight; and the existent is what can act and be acted upon. Then it is known that every beautiful thing is pleasant to hearing and to sight together, but what is pleasant to sight alone is beautiful, so it is beautiful and not beautiful. Likewise what is pleasant to hearing alone. In short, if each of them is a condition for correctness, then what is pleasant to sight, for example, would not be beautiful. And if it is not a condition, then one of them falls outside the essence of the definition and is superfluous. As for decrease, it is like when what specifies and distinguishes it is not included, as when it is said, for example, that wind is movement of air without saying how much, or that an earthquake is movement of the earth's body without saying how much and how; this goes back to omitting a differentia. It has been said in the first teaching (Topics) in this context that if a differentia among these differentiae is omitted, the essence of that thing is not described. This indicates that the correct doctrine is that the essence of that thing is only completed by the perfection of its essential attributes, and the genus alone does not indicate the essence of a single species. Among the examples for these topics is what was said in the definition of will: that it is an inclination of desire towards the good, and it is not said 'towards the good in appearance' because sometimes what is not truly good is willed. And this...
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is a systematic classification of errors in definition, focusing on excess (ziyada) and deficiency (nuqsan). The author explains that an error of increase occurs when the definition includes two mutually exclusive conditions, such as defining the beautiful as pleasant to both hearing and sight. This is problematic because if both are required, then something pleasant to only one would be excluded, yet we know such a thing is still beautiful. Conversely, if they are not both required, one condition is superfluous. The error of decrease occurs when the definition omits the specifying or distinguishing differentia, as in defining wind simply as 'movement of air' without specifying magnitude or direction, or defining earthquake as 'movement of the earth's body' without specifying its type. The author cites Aristotle's Topics to support that omitting a differentia fails to capture the essence. This demonstrates that the correct view is that essence is completed by all essential attributes, and the genus alone is insufficient. Another example given is the definition of will (al-irada) as 'inclination towards the good' — this is deficient because it does not specify that it is towards the apparent good, since sometimes evil is willed. The text ends mid-sentence, suggesting continuation.

Key Terms
الزيادة
النقصان
التعليم الأول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the error in defining 'will' as 'inclination of desire towards the good'?
A) It includes a superfluous condition (increase).
B) It omits the specifying differentia (decrease).
C) It confuses genus and differentia.
D) It uses a circular definition.

Key Takeaway
Definition errors of increase (adding unnecessary conditions) and decrease (omitting essential differentiae) both undermine the precision of a definition, and recognizing them is essential for sound reasoning in Islamic sciences.

?
Consider the definition of 'iman' (faith) as 'belief in the heart, utterance by the tongue, and action by the limbs.' How might this definition be vulnerable to an error of increase or decrease? Provide a brief analysis.

Error by Increase in Definition (زيادة)
Definition of increase error with examples of beauty and existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition contains a redundant condition that makes it too narrow, using the example of beauty being defined as pleasing to both hearing and sight.

Core Idea
Adding an unnecessary condition to a definition excludes valid instances — you define too narrowly.

The author begins by showing how definitions can go wrong by including too much. When an extra attribute is added that is not part of the essence, the definition fails to cover all true instances. This is the error of increase. We'll learn how to spot it and correct it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition given.
Find the term being defined and the conditions listed. E.g., 'the beautiful is what is pleasing to hearing and to sight'.
2
Check if the conditions are both necessary.
Are both conditions required for the thing to be what it is? Consider if something satisfying only one condition still qualifies as an instance.
3
Test with a counterexample.
Find something that satisfies only one condition but is still a valid instance. For beauty, something pleasing to sight alone is still beautiful.
4
Determine if the extra condition is redundant or exclusionary.
If the condition excludes true instances, it is an error by increase. If it adds nothing, it is also redundant.

Chapter: Among examples of these topics are errors in definition with respect to increase, decrease, the whole, the part, and combination with the conjunction 'and' and other things. As for increase, it is like introducing two correlative things in the definition, as when it is said that the beautiful is what is pleasing to hearing and what is pleasing to sight; and the existent is what can act and be acted upon. Then it is known that every beautiful thing is pleasing to both hearing and sight together, but what is pleasing to sight alone is beautiful, so it is beautiful and not beautiful. Likewise what is pleasing to hearing alone. In summary, if each of them were a condition for correctness, then what is pleasing to sight, for example, would not be beautiful. And if it were not a condition, then one of them would be outside the essence of the definition and thus redundant. As for decrease, it is like when the specifying and distinguishing factor is not introduced, as when it is said that wind is movement of air without specifying how much, or that an earthquake is movement of the earth's body without specifying its quantity and quality; this goes back to omitting a differentia. It was said in the First Teaching in this regard that if a differentia from among these differentiae is omitted, the essence of that thing is not described. This indicates that the correct doctrine is that the essence of that thing is only completed by the perfection of its own attributes, and that the genus alone does not indicate the essence of a single species. Among the examples for these topics is what was said in the definition of will: that it is an impulse of desire towards good, without saying 'towards perceived good', for sometimes what is not truly good is desired. This example differs from the first in that it makes the thing more general, while the former makes it more specific, for 'perceived good' is more general than 'good' meant as true good. This example is not valid according to the doctrine of the forms, for the true form according to them is only for what is true in itself. As for what is according to appearance, it is not taken for every form, so how can it exist in this way when it must exist for some things in their manner? Just as generality must be considered in the face of generality, likewise specificity must be considered in the face of specificity. As for what concerns the whole, part of the error is that the parts are mentioned in sequence with the conjunction 'and', and that is made a definition of the whole, as when it is said that justice is modesty, courage, and wisdom; for this makes modesty predicated of justice, and courage also predicated of it; so each one is predicated alone, not one restricted by the other. Thus it would not be like saying 'modesty which is courage', as it is said 'rational animal', i.e., the animal that is rational. In summary, it is invalid in all respects. Know that the whole arises from parts in three ways: first, by mere collection, however it happens, like four from its parts. Second, by an addition to the collection itself, entering into its quality, like a house. Third, by an addition to the collection and the form of the collection; that is, the parts have a state and a judgment after assembly that differs from the assembly and its form, in that it is a composition and collection, like a mixture. For after assembly and its form, a qualitative increase occurs. For what exists by mere collection, it suffices in its definition that it is such-and-such a collection. As for what is with increase, this does not suffice unless the form of that collection and other things are indicated. As for what pertains to the word 'with' from these topics, it is like when it is said...
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of errors in definition, based on Aristotle's Topics. The author identifies several types: increase, decrease, whole/part, and conjunction with 'and'. Each is illustrated with examples from logic and natural philosophy. The discussion begins with errors by increase, where two correlative conditions are introduced, making the definition too narrow. For instance, defining beauty as both pleasing to hearing and sight excludes things pleasing only to one sense. The error by decrease occurs when the differentia is omitted, e.g., defining wind as 'movement of air' without specifying direction or magnitude. This shows that the essence of a thing is completed by its full set of attributes; genus alone is insufficient. The example of defining will as 'impulse towards good' is criticized for being too general: it should specify 'perceived good' because people may desire what is not truly good. This illustrates the need for proper generality and specificity. Then, errors concerning the whole are discussed: defining a composite by listing its parts with 'and' without indicating their combination, e.g., defining justice as 'modesty, courage, and wisdom' implies each is predicated separately, not that justice is a unity of these. The correct definition would be like 'rational animal' where 'rational' restricts 'animal'. Finally, the author explains how wholes arise from parts: (1) mere collection (like the number four), (2) addition to the collection (like a house, where arrangement matters), and (3) addition and form of collection (like a mixture, where a new quality emerges). For each, the definition must correspond to the mode of composition. The text emphasizes that definitions must capture the essence precisely, avoiding excess or deficiency. This has direct application in Islamic sciences: for instance, in fiqh, defining 'salah' must include its essential pillars and conditions without adding superfluous elements or omitting necessary ones.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An error in definition where an extra condition or attribute is introduced, making the definition too narrow or redundant.
حد (hadd): Definition; a statement that captures the essence of a thing through its genus and differentia.
فصل (fasl): Differentia; the attribute that distinguishes a species within its genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the problem with defining 'the beautiful' as 'what is pleasing to hearing and to sight'?
A) It omits the differentia.
B) It adds a redundant condition that excludes true instances of beauty.
C) It defines by listing parts without specifying combination.
D) It uses the word 'and' incorrectly.

Key Takeaway
An error by increase introduces a condition that either is redundant or excludes true instances, making the definition too narrow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Sawm (fasting) is abstaining from food, drink, and sexual activity from dawn to sunset, with the intention to obey Allah.' Check if this definition contains any error of increase. Provide a counterexample if possible.
?
In a textbook on Islamic jurisprudence, you find: 'Zakat is the transfer of ownership of a specific portion of wealth to a poor person, with the condition that the wealth has been in one's possession for one lunar year.' Identify if there is any error of increase in this definition.

Error by Decrease in Definition (نقصان)
Definition of decrease error with examples of wind, earthquake, and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition omits a necessary differentia, making it too broad, using examples of wind, earthquake, and will.

Core Idea
Omitting the distinguishing attribute (differentia) makes the definition apply to too many things — you define too broadly.

The author next discusses errors by decrease: definitions that omit the specifying factor (differentia). Without it, the definition covers more than the intended term. For instance, defining wind as 'movement of air' without specifying direction or magnitude fails to distinguish it from other air movements. We'll explore how to detect and fix such omissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus in the definition.
Find the broader category. For wind, the genus is 'movement of air'.
2
Determine if a differentia is present.
A complete definition needs a differentia that specifies the unique feature. Here, it is missing.
3
Find a counterexample that fits the genus but not the intended term.
For wind: air movement from a fan or breath is also movement of air but not wind.
4
Propose the missing differentia.
What distinguishes wind? Possibly its natural occurrence and certain magnitude. Provide a corrected definition.

Chapter: Among examples of these topics are errors in definition with respect to increase, decrease, the whole, the part, and combination with the conjunction 'and' and other things. As for increase, it is like introducing two correlative things in the definition, as when it is said that the beautiful is what is pleasing to hearing and what is pleasing to sight; and the existent is what can act and be acted upon. Then it is known that every beautiful thing is pleasing to both hearing and sight together, but what is pleasing to sight alone is beautiful, so it is beautiful and not beautiful. Likewise what is pleasing to hearing alone. In summary, if each of them were a condition for correctness, then what is pleasing to sight, for example, would not be beautiful. And if it were not a condition, then one of them would be outside the essence of the definition and thus redundant. As for decrease, it is like when the specifying and distinguishing factor is not introduced, as when it is said that wind is movement of air without specifying how much, or that an earthquake is movement of the earth's body without specifying its quantity and quality; this goes back to omitting a differentia. It was said in the First Teaching in this regard that if a differentia from among these differentiae is omitted, the essence of that thing is not described. This indicates that the correct doctrine is that the essence of that thing is only completed by the perfection of its own attributes, and that the genus alone does not indicate the essence of a single species. Among the examples for these topics is what was said in the definition of will: that it is an impulse of desire towards good, without saying 'towards perceived good', for sometimes what is not truly good is desired. This example differs from the first in that it makes the thing more general, while the former makes it more specific, for 'perceived good' is more general than 'good' meant as true good. This example is not valid according to the doctrine of the forms, for the true form according to them is only for what is true in itself. As for what is according to appearance, it is not taken for every form, so how can it exist in this way when it must exist for some things in their manner? Just as generality must be considered in the face of generality, likewise specificity must be considered in the face of specificity. As for what concerns the whole, part of the error is that the parts are mentioned in sequence with the conjunction 'and', and that is made a definition of the whole, as when it is said that justice is modesty, courage, and wisdom; for this makes modesty predicated of justice, and courage also predicated of it; so each one is predicated alone, not one restricted by the other. Thus it would not be like saying 'modesty which is courage', as it is said 'rational animal', i.e., the animal that is rational. In summary, it is invalid in all respects. Know that the whole arises from parts in three ways: first, by mere collection, however it happens, like four from its parts. Second, by an addition to the collection itself, entering into its quality, like a house. Third, by an addition to the collection and the form of the collection; that is, the parts have a state and a judgment after assembly that differs from the assembly and its form, in that it is a composition and collection, like a mixture. For after assembly and its form, a qualitative increase occurs. For what exists by mere collection, it suffices in its definition that it is such-and-such a collection. As for what is with increase, this does not suffice unless the form of that collection and other things are indicated. As for what pertains to the word 'with' from these topics, it is like when it is said...
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of errors in definition, based on Aristotle's Topics. The author identifies several types: increase, decrease, whole/part, and conjunction with 'and'. Each is illustrated with examples from logic and natural philosophy. The discussion begins with errors by increase, where two correlative conditions are introduced, making the definition too narrow. For instance, defining beauty as both pleasing to hearing and sight excludes things pleasing only to one sense. The error by decrease occurs when the differentia is omitted, e.g., defining wind as 'movement of air' without specifying direction or magnitude. This shows that the essence of a thing is completed by its full set of attributes; genus alone is insufficient. The example of defining will as 'impulse towards good' is criticized for being too general: it should specify 'perceived good' because people may desire what is not truly good. This illustrates the need for proper generality and specificity. Then, errors concerning the whole are discussed: defining a composite by listing its parts with 'and' without indicating their combination, e.g., defining justice as 'modesty, courage, and wisdom' implies each is predicated separately, not that justice is a unity of these. The correct definition would be like 'rational animal' where 'rational' restricts 'animal'. Finally, the author explains how wholes arise from parts: (1) mere collection (like the number four), (2) addition to the collection (like a house, where arrangement matters), and (3) addition and form of collection (like a mixture, where a new quality emerges). For each, the definition must correspond to the mode of composition. The text emphasizes that definitions must capture the essence precisely, avoiding excess or deficiency. This has direct application in Islamic sciences: for instance, in fiqh, defining 'salah' must include its essential pillars and conditions without adding superfluous elements or omitting necessary ones.

Key Terms
نقصان (nuqsan): An error in definition where a necessary distinguishing attribute (differentia) is omitted, making the definition too broad.
فصل (fasl): Differentia; the attribute that distinguishes a species within its genus.
جنس (jins): Genus; the broader category that encompasses the species.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which error does the definition 'wind is movement of air' commit according to the passage?
A) Error by increase (زيادة)
B) Error by decrease (نقصان)
C) Error concerning the whole (الكل)
D) Error with the word 'with' (مع)

Key Takeaway
An error by decrease omits the differentia, making the definition too broad and failing to capture the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Shirk (associating partners with Allah) is worshipping other beings.' Identify the genus and missing differentia. Suggest a complete definition.
?
In a kalam text, you find: 'The soul (ruh) is a subtle body penetrating the physical body.' Check if this definition suffers from decrease (i.e., is the differentia present? What distinguishes it from other subtle bodies?).
